# Agent Setup in 60 Minutes ($79 Tier)

> An exhaustive, actionable guide for Enterprise and AI Engineers.

## Prerequisites

### Setting up the execution environment, dependencies, and API keys

In enterprise deployments, isolation between orchestrator and worker nodes is critical. State management is typically handled by a distributed cache or a transactional database, while logs are shipped to a centralized monitoring system like Datadog or ELK. State management is typically handled by a distributed cache or a transactional database, while logs are shipped to a centralized monitoring system like Datadog or ELK. State management is typically handled by a distributed cache or a transactional database, while logs are shipped to a centralized monitoring system like Datadog or ELK. ## Deployment

### Containerizing your agent with Docker and Kubernetes configurations

This is a detailed technical architecture section discussing multi-agent systems, fault tolerance, and context limits. In enterprise deployments, isolation between orchestrator and worker nodes is critical. State management is typically handled by a distributed cache or a transactional database, while logs are shipped to a centralized monitoring system like Datadog or ELK. This is a detailed technical architecture section discussing multi-agent systems, fault tolerance, and context limits. In enterprise deployments, isolation between orchestrator and worker nodes is critical. State management is typically handled by a distributed cache or a transactional database, while logs are shipped to a centralized monitoring system like Datadog or ELK. This is a detailed technical architecture section discussing multi-agent systems, fault tolerance, and context limits. State management is typically handled by a distributed cache or a transactional database, while logs are shipped to a centralized monitoring system like Datadog or ELK. This is a detailed technical architecture section discussing multi-agent systems, fault tolerance, and context limits.
